\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                                      \u2502 Batch Storage   \u2502   \u2502 Single Batch \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                                               \u2502                    \u2502\n                                               \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                                                      \u2502\n                                                      \u25bc\n                                            \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                                            \u2502  Mint-Factory   \u2502\n                                            \u2502 (Parallel Batch \u2502\n                                            \u2502  Processing)    \u2502\n                                            \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                                                     \u2502\n                                                     \u25bc\n                                            \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                                            \u2502 Gallery-Gateway \u2502\n                                            \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### 3.2 New Data Flow\n\n#### Phase 1: Intent Collection (Off-Chain)\n\n1. User mint requests are published to a new high-throughput Kafka topic: `mint-intent.queue`\n2. A new **Batch Aggregator Service** consumes from this topic\n3. Aggregator collects mint intents for a configurable window (e.g., 2 seconds or 500 intents)\n4. For each batch:\n   - Computes a Merkle tree of all mint intent hashes\n   - Stores the full batch data off-chain (IPFS, S3, or side-chain database)\n   - Records the CID/location reference\n\n#### Phase 2: Batch Commitment (On-Chain)\n\n5. Aggregator submits a **single transaction** to LedgerCore containing:\n   - Merkle root of the batch\n   - Batch size count\n   - Reference to off-chain data (IPFS CID)\n6. LedgerCore processes this **one transaction** through consensus (instead of hundreds)\n7. Block is finalized and `batch.finalized` event is emitted\n\n#### Phase 3: Parallel Processing (Mint-Factory)\n\n8. Mint-Factory receives `batch.finalized` event\n9. Retrieves full batch data from off-chain storage\n10. **Parallelizes** artifact generation across multiple worker threads/processes\n11. Each worker generates artifacts and emits individual `artifact.minted` events\n\n### 3.3 Benefits\n\n| Metric | Current Architecture | Proposed Architecture |\n|--------|---------------------|----------------------|\n| Consensus Transactions | N (one per mint) | 1 (one per batch) |\n| Consensus Throughput | ~10-50 TPS | ~5,000-50,000 mints/batch |\n| Block Finalization Wait | Per-transaction | Per-batch |\n| Mint-Factory Processing | Serial | Parallel |\n| Peak Latency | Minutes | Seconds |\n\n### 3.4 Trade-offs\n\n| Aspect | Trade-off |\n|--------|-----------|\n| **Individual Latency** | Slight increase (~2 seconds) for batching window; individual mints must wait for batch aggregation |\n| **Complexity** | New Batch Aggregator service; off-chain storage dependency; Merkle proof verification |\n| **Data Consistency** | Eventual consistency within batch; users see \"pending\" state until batch finalizes |\n| **Recovery** | More complex failure recovery; need to handle partial batch failures |\n| **Cost** | Additional infrastructure (IPFS/S3); but reduced on-chain storage per-mint |\n| **Atomicity** | Batch commits atomically; individual mint failures must be handled separately |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Key Files and Components Requiring Modification\n\n### 4.1 New Service: Batch Aggregator\n\n**Location:** `services/batch_aggregator/` (new)\n\n| File | Component | Modification submitted_at = 5;\n}\n\nmessage CanvasEvent {\n    // ... existing fields ...\n    oneof body {\n        // ... existing types ...\n        BatchCommit batch_commit = 15;  // NEW\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### `gallery_query_get_artifact()` | Handle batch-minted artifacts with \"pending\" state |\n| 144-157 | LRU cache | Increase cache capacity for burst loads |\n| 50-52 | TTL constants | Reduce TTL during protocol | Define Merkle proof structures |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Implementation Considerations\n\n### 5.1 Batch Window Tuning\n\nThe batch aggregation window should be configurable:\n- **Time-based:** Aggregate for N milliseconds (e.g., 1000-2000ms)\n- **Count-based:** Aggregate up to M intents (e.g., 500-1000)\n- **Hybrid:** Whichever threshold is reached first\n\n### 5.2 Merkle Proof Verification\n\nFor disputes or individual artifact verification:\n- Store Merkle proofs alongside batch data\n- Allow clients to verify inclusion without full batch retrieval\n\n### 5.3 Failure Handling\n\n- **Partial batch failure:** Log failed mints, continue with successful ones\n- **Storage failure:** Retry with exponential backoff; fallback to synchronous mode\n- **Consensus failure:** Re-submit batch transaction\n\n### 5.4 Migration Strategy\n\n1. Deploy Batch Aggregator as optional parallel path\n2. Route percentage of traffic through batch path (A/B testing)\n3. Monitor latency and throughput metrics\n4. Gradually increase batch path traffic\n5. Deprecate direct mint path once stable\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\nThe HoloCanvas minting bottleneck stems from the **serial, synchronous block processing** in LedgerCore's consensus layer, exacerbated by the global mutex in transaction processing. The proposed batch aggregation architecture addresses this by:\n\n1. **Reducing consensus load** from N transactions to 1 per batch\n2. **Enabling parallel artifact generation** in Mint-Factory\n3. **Decoupling** on-chain commitment from off-chain artifact data\n\nWhile introducing additional complexity and a slight latency increase for individual mints, this architecture can improve peak throughput by **100-1000x**, transforming multi-minute delays into sub-10-second response times during evolution events.\n",

  "content": "# HoloCanvas Architectural Bottleneck Analysis for NFT Minting Throughput\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis document presents a comprehensive architectural analysis of the HoloCanvas NFT minting system, identifies the primary performance bottleneck causing latency during peak load, and proposes a high-level architectural modification to improve throughput.\n\n---\n\n## 1. End-to-End Minting Data Flow Analysis\n\n### 1.1 Overview\n\nHoloCanvas is a C-based microservice ecosystem that orchestrates the minting, governance, and market evolution of generative NFTs. The services communicate through **Kafka** event streams and **gRPC** contracts, as documented in `ARCHITECTURE.md:27-28`.\n\n### 1.2 Complete Minting Lifecycle\n\nThe minting flow traverses the following services:\n\n```\nUser \u2192 Wallet-Proxy \u2192 LedgerCore \u2192 Consensus \u2192 Mint-Factory \u2192 Gallery-Gateway\n```\n\n#### Step 1: User Request Entry (Wallet-Proxy)\n\n**File:** `services/wallet_proxy/src/proxy_server.c`\n\nThe user initiates a mint request through the Wallet-Proxy, which provides:\n- Wallet creation using Ed25519 key pairs (`proxy_server.c:258-290`)\n- Transaction signing (`proxy_server.c:332-400`)\n- Transaction broadcast to LedgerCore (`proxy_server.c:402-443`)\n\nThe `handle_tx_broadcast()` function at line 402 calls `ledger_broadcast_transaction()` to forward signed transactions to LedgerCore.\n\n#### Step 2: Transaction Processing (LedgerCore)\n\n**Files:**\n- `services/ledger_core/src/transaction_processor.c`\n- `services/ledger_core/src/block_builder.c`\n- `services/ledger_core/src/consensus_manager.c`\n\n**Transaction Processor (`transaction_processor.c:147-200`):**\n\nThe `tp_process()` function handles incoming transactions through a synchronous validation pipeline:\n1. **Decode** - Deserializes the transaction (`tx_decode()`)\n2. **Signature Verification** - Ed25519 signature verification (`tp_verify_signature()` at line 209-232)\n3. **Nonce Verification** - Anti-replay protection (`tp_verify_nonce()` at line 238-252)\n4. **Funds Verification** - Balance validation (`tp_verify_funds()` at line 257-275)\n5. **State Application** - Mutates ledger state under a **global mutex** (`tp_apply()` at line 288-352)\n\nCritical observation from `transaction_processor.c:286-287`:\n```c\n/* NOTE: called inside the global mutex for now. In production deployments\n   we may employ sharded, fine-grained locks or MVCC to improve throughput. */\n```\n\n**Block Builder (`block_builder.c:147-222`):**\n\nThe block builder runs in a dedicated worker thread that:\n1. Monitors the mempool for pending transactions\n2. Triggers block creation based on:\n   - Transaction count threshold (`cfg.max_txs_per_block`)\n   - Time-based interval (`cfg.max_block_interval_ms`)\n3. Builds a Merkle tree of transactions (`compute_merkle_root()` at line 279-322)\n4. Submits candidate blocks to the consensus engine (`consensus_submit_block()` at line 204)\n\n**Consensus Manager (`consensus_manager.c:297-357`):**\n\nThe consensus manager's worker loop (`_worker_loop()`) processes blocks **sequentially**:\n1. Dequeues a candidate block (`_dequeue_block()`)\n2. **Verifies** the block via pluggable consensus engine (`engine.verify_block()` at line 308)\n3. **Finalizes** state transitions (`engine.finalise_block()` at line 320)\n4. **Commits** to durable storage (`ledger_storage_put_block()` at line 333)\n5. **Publishes** \"ledger.block.finalised\" event to Kafka (`event_bus_publish()` at line 344)\n\n#### Step 3: Consensus Engine (PoS Strategy)\n\n**File:** `services/ledger_core/src/strategies/pos_strategy.c`\n\nThe Proof-of-Stake consensus plugin (`pos_strategy.c`) performs:\n- Validator selection via VRF (`vrf_elect()` at line 427-463)\n- Block verification (`crypto_verify_block()`)\n- Reward distribution (`apply_block_rewards()` at line 472-505)\n\nThe `pos_strategy_handle_block()` function (line 273-312) validates blocks synchronously, verifying signatures and proposer eligibility **for each block**.\n\n#### Step 4: Event Propagation to Mint-Factory\n\n**File:** `services/mint_factory/src/event_handler.c`\n\nThe Mint-Factory's event handler subscribes to Kafka topics and consumes events in a dedicated thread (`run_loop()` at line 201-248):\n- Parses incoming JSON events (`parse_event()` at line 262-319)\n- Dispatches to appropriate handlers based on event type:\n  - `EVT_MINT_REQUEST` \u2192 `mint_engine_handle_request()` (line 340)\n  - `EVT_BID` \u2192 `mint_engine_handle_bid()` (line 345)\n\n**Key Configuration from `event_handler.c:55-60`:**\n```c\n#define KAFKA_TOPICS \"mint-factory.events\"\n#define KAFKA_CONSUMER_POLL_TIMEOUT_MS 250\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Artifact Generation (Mint-Factory)\n\n**Files:**\n- `services/mint_factory/src/recipe_composer.c`\n- `services/mint_factory/src/artifact_factory.c`\n\n**Recipe Composer (`recipe_composer.c`):**\n- Assembles creative fragments (shader, audio, metadata) into canonical JSON\n- Computes SHA-256 hash for deterministic artifact ID\n- **Synchronously persists** to disk and optionally emits Kafka event\n\n**Artifact Factory (`artifact_factory.c:176-252`):**\n\nThe `af_mint()` function performs:\n1. Fragment validation (`validate_fragments()`)\n2. JSON recipe composition (`compose_recipe_json()`)\n3. SHA-256 ID generation (`sha256_hex()`)\n4. **Synchronous persistence** to LedgerCore (`persist_to_ledger()` at line 219)\n5. Event emission (\"ArtifactMinted\" to `artifact.events` topic at line 238)\n\n#### Step 6: Gallery Update (Gallery-Gateway)\n\n**File:** `services/gallery_gateway/src/query_service.c`\n\nThe query service maintains an LRU cache and federates data from LedgerCore:\n- `gallery_query_get_artifact()` (line 459-510) retrieves artifact state\n- Cache TTL: 5 minutes (`DEFAULT_CACHE_TTL_SEC` at line 52)\n- Falls back to HTTP GET from LedgerCore endpoint\n\n### 1.3 Kafka Topic Configuration\n\n**File:** `config/kafka_topics.json`\n\nKey topics in the minting flow:\n| Topic | Purpose | Partitions |\n|-------|---------|------------|\n| `ledgercore.tx.incoming` | Raw transactions to LedgerCore | 9 |\n| `mint-factory.request` | Minting requests | 12 |\n| `mint-factory.artifact.minted` | Successful mint notifications | 3 |\n| `consensus.block.finalized` | Block finalization events | 3 |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Architectural Bottleneck Identification\n\n### 2.1 Primary Bottleneck: Serial Block Processing in LedgerCore Consensus\n\nThe **primary scalability bottleneck** is the **serial, synchronous block processing** in the LedgerCore consensus layer.\n\n#### Evidence:\n\n**1. Single-threaded Consensus Worker (`consensus_manager.c:297-357`):**\n\n```c\nstatic void *_worker_loop(void *arg)\n{\n    consensus_manager_t *mgr = arg;\n    for (;;) {\n        block_t *blk = _dequeue_block(mgr);  // BLOCKING dequeue\n        if (!blk) break;\n\n        // Step 1: Verify candidate block - SYNCHRONOUS\n        if (!mgr->engine.verify_block(blk, &err_msg)) { ... }\n\n        // Step 2: Finalise - SYNCHRONOUS\n        if (!mgr->engine.finalise_block(blk, new_state_root, &err_msg)) { ... }\n\n        // Step 3: Commit to storage - SYNCHRONOUS\n        if (!ledger_storage_put_block(mgr->storage, blk) || ...) { ... }\n\n        // Step 4: Publish event - only AFTER all above complete\n        event_bus_publish(mgr->event_bus, \"ledger.block.finalised\", blk, sizeof(*blk));\n    }\n}\n```\n\nBlocks are processed **one at a time**, serially. Each block must be fully verified, finalized, and committed before the next block can be processed.\n\n**2. Global Mutex in Transaction Processor (`transaction_processor.c:286-352`):**\n\n```c\nstatic int tp_apply(txp_ctx_t *ctx, const tx_t *tx, uint64_t ts_unix)\n{\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&ctx->mtx);  // GLOBAL LOCK\n\n    /* All ledger mutations happen here under a single lock */\n    ledger_append(ctx->ledger, &entry);\n    ledger_inc_nonce(ctx->ledger, tx->from);\n    ledger_debit(ctx->ledger, tx->from, ...);\n    ledger_credit(ctx->ledger, tx->to, tx->value);\n\n    /* Domain-specific mutations also serialized */\n    switch (tx->type) {\n        case TX_MINT_NFT:\n            artifact_state_on_mint(ctx->ledger, &tx->payload.mint);\n            break;\n        // ...\n    }\n\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&ctx->mtx);\n}\n```\n\nThe code explicitly acknowledges this limitation in the comment: *\"In production deployments we may employ sharded, fine-grained locks or MVCC to improve throughput.\"*\n\n**3. Per-Block Consensus Overhead (`pos_strategy.c:273-312`):**\n\nEach block requires:\n- Cryptographic signature verification (`crypto_verify_block()`)\n- Validator lookup and state validation\n- VRF-based proposer selection for the next block\n- Reward distribution calculations\n\n**4. Sequential Kafka Event Publishing:**\n\nThe `ledger.block.finalised` event is only published **after** all synchronous operations complete. Downstream services (Mint-Factory, Gallery-Gateway) cannot proceed until this event arrives.\n\n### 2.2 Secondary Bottleneck: Synchronous Artifact Generation\n\nThe Mint-Factory's artifact generation is also synchronous:\n\n**`artifact_factory.c:218-224`:**\n```c\n/* Persist recipe to LedgerCore */\nif (!persist_to_ledger(artifact_id, recipe_str))\n{\n    HC_LOG_ERROR(\"artifact_factory: failed to persist artifact to ledger\");\n    free(recipe_str);\n    return AF_STATUS_ERR_DEPENDENCY;\n}\n```\n\nThis creates a **synchronous round-trip** back to LedgerCore for each mint, compounding the consensus bottleneck.\n\n### 2.3 Impact During Peak Load\n\nDuring \"evolution events\" triggered by Muse-Observer:\n1. A surge of mint requests floods `ledgercore.tx.incoming`\n2. Transactions queue in the mempool waiting for block inclusion\n3. Block builder creates candidate blocks\n4. Consensus processes blocks **one at a time**\n5. Each block finalization creates backpressure\n6. Mint-Factory waits for block finalization events\n7. Gallery-Gateway waits for artifact creation events\n8. Users experience minutes of latency instead of seconds\n\n---\n\n## 3. Proposed Architectural Solution: Batch Aggregation with Off-Chain Pre-Commitment\n\n### 3.1 High-Level Design\n\nTransform the one-by-one transaction model into a **batch aggregation** architecture using an off-chain pre-commitment queue.\n\n```\n                     \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n                                         \u2502 Gallery-Gateway \u2502\n                                            \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### 3.2 New Data Flow\n\n#### Phase 1: Intent Collection (Off-Chain)\n\n1. User mint requests are published to a new high-throughput Kafka topic: `mint-intent.queue`\n2. A new **Batch Aggregator Service** consumes from this topic\n3. Aggregator collects mint intents for a configurable window (e.g., 2 seconds or 500 intents)\n4. For each batch:\n   - Computes a Merkle tree of all mint intent hashes\n   - Stores the full batch data off-chain (IPFS, S3, or side-chain database)\n   - Records the CID/location reference\n\n#### Phase 2: Batch Commitment (On-Chain)\n\n5. Aggregator submits a **single transaction** to LedgerCore containing:\n   - Merkle root of the batch\n   - Batch size count\n   - Reference to off-chain data (IPFS CID)\n6. LedgerCore processes this **one transaction** through consensus (instead of hundreds)\n7. Block is finalized and `batch.finalized` event is emitted\n\n#### Phase 3: Parallel Processing (Mint-Factory)\n\n8. Mint-Factory receives `batch.finalized` event\n9. Retrieves full batch data from off-chain storage\n10. **Parallelizes** artifact generation across multiple worker threads/processes\n11. Each worker generates artifacts and emits individual `artifact.minted` events\n\n### 3.3 Benefits\n\n| Metric | Current Architecture | Proposed Architecture |\n|--------|---------------------|----------------------|\n| Consensus Transactions | N (one per mint) | 1 (one per batch) |\n| Consensus Throughput | ~10-50 TPS | ~5,000-50,000 mints/batch |\n| Block Finalization Wait | Per-transaction | Per-batch |\n| Mint-Factory Processing | Serial | Parallel |\n| Peak Latency | Minutes | Seconds |\n\n### 3.4 Trade-offs\n\n| Aspect | Trade-off |\n|--------|-----------|\n| **Individual Latency** | Slight increase (~2 seconds) for batching window; individual mints must wait for batch aggregation |\n| **Complexity** | New Batch Aggregator service; off-chain storage dependency; Merkle proof verification |\n| **Data Consistency** | Eventual consistency within batch; users see \"pending\" state until batch finalizes |\n| **Recovery** | More complex failure recovery; need to handle partial batch failures |\n| **Cost** | Additional infrastructure (IPFS/S3); but reduced on-chain storage per-mint |\n| **Atomicity** | Batch commits atomically; individual mint failures must be handled separately |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Implementation Considerations\n\n### 5.1 Batch Window Tuning\n\nThe batch aggregation window should be configurable:\n- **Time-based:** Aggregate for N milliseconds (e.g., 1000-2000ms)\n- **Count-based:** Aggregate up to M intents (e.g., 500-1000)\n- **Hybrid:** Whichever threshold is reached first\n\n### 5.2 Merkle Proof Verification\n\nFor disputes or individual artifact verification:\n- Store Merkle proofs alongside batch data\n- Allow clients to verify inclusion without full batch retrieval\n\n### 5.3 Failure Handling\n\n- **Partial batch failure:** Log failed mints, continue with successful ones\n- **Storage failure:** Retry with exponential backoff; fallback to synchronous mode\n- **Consensus failure:** Re-submit batch transaction\n\n### 5.4 Migration Strategy\n\n1. Deploy Batch Aggregator as optional parallel path\n2. Route percentage of traffic through batch path (A/B testing)\n3. Monitor latency and throughput metrics\n4. Gradually increase batch path traffic\n5. Deprecate direct mint path once stable\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\nThe HoloCanvas minting bottleneck stems from the **serial, synchronous block processing** in LedgerCore's consensus layer, exacerbated by the global mutex in transaction processing. The proposed batch aggregation architecture addresses this by:\n\n1. **Reducing consensus load** from N transactions to 1 per batch\n2. **Enabling parallel artifact generation** in Mint-Factory\n3. **Decoupling** on-chain commitment from off-chain artifact data\n\nWhile introducing additional complexity and a slight latency increase for individual mints, this architecture can improve peak throughput by **100-1000x**, transforming multi-minute delays into sub-10-second response times during evolution events.\n",

# HoloCanvas Architectural Bottleneck Analysis for NFT Minting Throughput

## Executive Summary

This document presents a comprehensive architectural analysis of the HoloCanvas NFT minting system, identifies the primary performance bottleneck causing latency during peak load, and proposes a high-level architectural modification to improve throughput.

---

## 1. End-to-End Minting Data Flow Analysis

### 1.1 Overview

HoloCanvas is a C-based microservice ecosystem that orchestrates the minting, governance, and market evolution of generative NFTs. The services communicate through **Kafka** event streams and **gRPC** contracts, as documented in `ARCHITECTURE.md:27-28`.

### 1.2 Complete Minting Lifecycle

The minting flow traverses the following services:

```
User → Wallet-Proxy → LedgerCore → Consensus → Mint-Factory → Gallery-Gateway
```

#### Step 1: User Request Entry (Wallet-Proxy)

**File:** `services/wallet_proxy/src/proxy_server.c`

The user initiates a mint request through the Wallet-Proxy, which provides:
- Wallet creation using Ed25519 key pairs (`proxy_server.c:258-290`)
- Transaction signing (`proxy_server.c:332-400`)
- Transaction broadcast to LedgerCore (`proxy_server.c:402-443`)

The `handle_tx_broadcast()` function at line 402 calls `ledger_broadcast_transaction()` to forward signed transactions to LedgerCore.

#### Step 2: Transaction Processing (LedgerCore)

**Files:**
- `services/ledger_core/src/transaction_processor.c`
- `services/ledger_core/src/block_builder.c`
- `services/ledger_core/src/consensus_manager.c`

**Transaction Processor (`transaction_processor.c:147-200`):**

The `tp_process()` function handles incoming transactions through a synchronous validation pipeline:
1. **Decode** - Deserializes the transaction (`tx_decode()`)
2. **Signature V
